ProVerif 2.05 run — chat-handshake-reconnect.pv (reconnect mode + Reject branch)
DCS98 chat reconnect-hardening v4, Task F.1 (GATES Task 2.4 — the Reject impl)
Date: 2026-06-09   Branch: feat/reconnect-hardening-v4

VERDICT (all 8 RESULT lines; see full transcript below):
  RESULT inj-event(R_commit_I_rc(a,b,t)) ==> inj-event(I_running_R_rc(a,b,t)) cannot be proved.
  RESULT (but event(R_commit_I_rc(a,b,t)) ==> event(I_running_R_rc(a,b,t)) is true.)
  RESULT event(R_commit_I_rc(a,b,t)) ==> event(I_running_R_rc(a,b,t)) is true.
  RESULT inj-event(I_commit_R_rc(a,b,t)) ==> inj-event(R_running_I_rc(a,b,t)) is true.
  RESULT event(I_retry_with(rpk,op)) ==> event(R_sent_reject(rpk,th,op)) is true.
  RESULT not attacker(s_id[]) is true.
  RESULT not attacker(s_rk[]) is true.
  RESULT not attacker(s_retry[]) is true.

READING:
  - R1a (R authenticates I): injective CANNOT be proved, but NON-INJECTIVE IS TRUE.
    This is the EXPECTED, documented outcome — identical to first_contact
    (chat-handshake.pv): there is no R-fresh nonce in TH1, so injective
    replay-freedom on the R<-I direction rests on durable one-time-prekey
    consumption, which is lifted in CryptoVerif, not ProVerif. NOT a defect.
  - R1b (I authenticates R): INJECTIVE agreement IS TRUE (TH3 folds R's fresh
    xeR and hs_type(MSG2), pinning the accept branch and giving replay-freedom).
  - R2 (recovery soundness): I_retry_with ==> R_sent_reject IS TRUE — I only
    ever retries against a prekey offered in a Reject the honest R genuinely
    produced (no forged/synthesised Reject can redirect I).
  - Secrecy s_id / s_rk / s_retry ALL TRUE — identity payload, reconnect root
    key, and the retry-path sentinel all stay secret. s_retry secrecy is the
    anti-redirect/anti-forge probe: a bogus Reject pointing I at an attacker
    prekey would leak s_retry; it does not.

DOWNGRADE / NON-SUBSTITUTION (Sig_R vs Sig_R_reject, mode, hs_type, last-resort):
  Exercised constructively, not by a separate event. The cross-mode
  firstContactSigner puts a genuine first_contact Sig_R (DS_HS_RESP) on the wire
  under the SAME is_R key; both reconnect accept (DS_HS_RESP over TH3 incl.
  hs_type(MSG2)) and reject (DS_HS_REJECT over TH_R0) branches are attacker-
  reachable. If the distinct DS prefixes did NOT separate accept from reject, an
  attacker could lift a Sig_R onto a Reject frame (=> I_retry_with fires for an
  op the honest R never rejected => R2 FAILS) or a Sig_R_reject onto an accept
  (=> I_commit_R_rc injective FAILS). Both R2 and R1b-injective PROVING is
  therefore the non-substitution + no-mode/hs_type/last-resort-coercion proof.

NOT PROVED HERE (stated honestly, per charter + spec):
  DoS AVAILABILITY / 'unconfirmed-R-never-blocks' / 'no-worse-than-HIGH-1' are
  LIVENESS properties ProVerif does not decide — NOT faked as a query. The
  enforcement bootstrap is modelled faithfully (confirmed + unconfirmed responder
  copies both at top level) and the SAFETY consequence IS shown: the unconfirmed
  (fail-open / ungated) responder path still satisfies auth + secrecy (it shares
  the same proven queries). Availability is argued in the spec (s3/s6).
